  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_01256cda-6b4e-491c-b348-ac9f43c95e03'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_170824273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170824273" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170824273?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780761374084" href="/book/show/10634910-ultraviolet">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Madeleine L'Engle and Ray Bradbury</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2011-favorites">2011-favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170824273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18341725659855650638"><b>Oh! This is <i>so cool</i>.</b>That was my reaction late last night when I finished this book and the feeling hasn't worn off. <i>Ultraviolet</i> is one of those sneaky books that makes you think you're reading one thing and then all the sudden, whoosh, you're off on a different adventure. I think many of us who spend a lot of time in the paranormal genre have come to expect a certain story structure from these types of books, but this one has no problem bending all the rules and leaping out to explore other dime</span>
  <span id="freeText18341725659855650638" style="display:none"><b>Oh! This is <i>so cool</i>.</b>That was my reaction late last night when I finished this book and the feeling hasn't worn off. <i>Ultraviolet</i> is one of those sneaky books that makes you think you're reading one thing and then all the sudden, whoosh, you're off on a different adventure. I think many of us who spend a lot of time in the paranormal genre have come to expect a certain story structure from these types of books, but this one has no problem bending all the rules and leaping out to explore other dimensions. Be careful as reviews start to come in, however, because the less you know about this story, the more you'll enjoy it.<br /><br />The book starts off with a bang: Alison has been institutionalized in a teen mental facility because she's confessed to killing Tori, a girl from school. The problem is, Ali watched her classmate disintegrate in front of her...and the body has disappeared. Since Ali's also seeing colors and tasting lies, she doesn't know whether she's really going crazy or not. She is isolated from her friends and family, she can't relate to the other kids in the facility, and she's being pressured by the police and her psychiatrist to give up information she knows will hurt her. The only one she can turn to is the handsome Dr. Faraday, who helps her understand her <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synesthesia" rel="nofollow noopener">synesthesia</a>, an unusual neurological condition in which she processes certain letters as colors, sees symbols where they don't exist, etc. <br /><br />The author spends a lot of time carefully easing us into a familiarity with Alison's condition and making us feel for her situation, and for the longest time I wasn't even sure if she was ever going to make it out of the institution since her mother keeps finding excuses to not to see her. It took me a little while to adjust to her condition as well, but once I settled in I really enjoyed seeing the world through Ali's sensations, even though I wasn't sure where the story was going. <br /><br />And then...just as you're getting comfortable, the author turns everything on its head. Shortly before it happened, I guessed what was going on--but the reveal is so simply and beautifully done that my little heart still fluttered. From that point on, the story kicks into high gear as Alison tries to solve the mystery of what happened to her classmate and to prove--and to <i>believe</i>--that she isn't insane at all. <br /><br />There is a wondrous moment near the end that made me catch my breath that invokes the same sort of feelings I get from lying in a meadow under a giant nightscape of stars and sky--that awesome, bigger-than-life emotion of gazing up into a beauty and mystery that we will never fully understand. It's hard to go into detail here about what made this book so fantastic for me without spoiling it, but as I was reading this scene, I flashed back to the very best work of Madeleine L'Engle and Ray Bradbury. I've often wondered if those two masters of speculative fiction are as beloved by teens today as they were back in the day, because like <i>Ultraviolet</i>, their work trusted their readers enough to peel back their many layers slowly and patiently. <br /><br />I'm not sure how this book will be viewed by modern mass audiences, but I do believe (and hope) that it's going to be critically very well received. It's intelligently written fiction with ideas that stimulate the imagination and move you with what's unspoken...as well as the infinite possibilities of a future yet to come.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2011/05/ultraviolet-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher for this review. </i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18341725659855650638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16086260604951246083">tommy has been telling me about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/171020.A_Mango_Shaped_Space' title='A Mango-Shaped Space by Wendy Mass' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Mango-Shaped Space</a> for a long time now, and after reading this, i both want to read that book and also to have synesthesia myself, please. it's like having a superpower that doesn't require you, morally, to go out and save the world. it is more like being on a mild acid trip all the time, without any of the accompanying backaches and food-aversion.<br/><br/>of course, in this book, her synesthesia is compounded with other special gifts which both complicate her life and a</span>
  <span id="freeText16086260604951246083" style="display:none">tommy has been telling me about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/171020.A_Mango_Shaped_Space" title="A Mango-Shaped Space by Wendy Mass" rel="nofollow noopener">A Mango-Shaped Space</a> for a long time now, and after reading this, i both want to read that book and also to have synesthesia myself, please. it's like having a superpower that doesn't require you, morally, to go out and save the world. it is more like being on a mild acid trip all the time, without any of the accompanying backaches and food-aversion.<br><br>of course, in this book, her synesthesia is compounded with other special gifts which both complicate her life and also give her additional abilities that regular synesthetes do not get to experience, but i will even take the traditional synesthesia effects, if there is a bored and license-revoked neurosurgeon out there who wants to make a quick ten bucks.i think it would make the world a richer and more entertaining place for me. and when i was stuck in a small-talk situation, i would at least have something to taste and other things to look at while i stood there, instead of feeling frantically trapped as i do.<br><br>i liked this book, but i wish i loved it as much as so many other people did.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ i'm not sure if i would have liked this more if the twist had been a complete surprise to me. because even though i didn't know it was going to be what it was, i knew that there <i>was</i> a twist, and that it was of a paranormal nature. and so i figured out what it was pretty early on, not because i am so smart and perceptive, but the clues are there, and if you know it is planning on going that route, it is easier to see them for what they are than when you think you are just reading a teen murder mystery/possibly psychotic protagonist book. i think if i had read this without knowing a single thing, the surprise of what happened would have been more exciting, you know? which is why i am putting all this in a spoiler, even though it is only a spoiler saying that maybe i was spoiled!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>but all of that is just to say i am a terrible book rater. i have book synesthesia - after reading a book, i just "see" the number of stars my purely emotional gut will give it. sometimes i try to be better, more objective, and give a book merit-based stars instead of karen's feeeelings, but then i remember i am not getting paid for this, and my feeeeelings are as good a barometer as any for determining a book's enjoyability to others, and i feel uneasy when i give a star-rating that i don't "feel". it grates on me.<br><br>and it is enjoyable - this is a really high three.i liked the pacing and the characters, i liked the storyline; it just didn't punch me in the soul or do for me what i need my fours to do for me. <br><br>and i liked the relationship, even though it was inappropriate for at least three reasons. but it's totally understandable. and i would obviously have had a crush on him, too, in her position. or even in my position, as a reader of the book. he sounds like my type, except for the whole, you know, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[alien <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> part. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[i don't do long-distance relationships well <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>i also liked the part at the end, when she is ummm... overtaxed? and she is coming to terms with and understanding the different influences in her life and what she took from each person to become the girl she was. and how she hated all of those influences. or not the individuals, you understand, but that she took the wrong messages from them and became someone she regretted.<br><br>it is definitely worth your time, unless you are someone with a much more important job than mine, like AIDS research or immortality studies or a plant that grows brie. you people shouldn't be reading anything at all, so get back to work.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer8640883528912279352">I've written a lot of stories, but ULTRAVIOLET is one of the very closest to my heart. It was also one of the hardest and most demanding things I've ever written, but thanks to the help of numerous smart critique partners, a tirelessly supportive agent and two wonderful editors, I can look at it now and say, "Yes. There it is. THAT is what I meant." I love this book very much, and I hope you will too.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_467325622" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467325622" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467325622?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780761374084" href="/book/show/10634910-ultraviolet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467325622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4108614888568538293"><b>3 1/2 stars</b><br/><br/>I know a whole bunch of my GR friends have heard me say this before but I'm going to say it again for the benefit of any newcomers who stumble across this review: because rating a book can be a tricky process and three stars can mean anything from "I was totally unmoved by it" to "it was pretty good for the most part", I tend to take the GR system literally. By this I mean that three stars is "I liked it" and is a mostly positive rating. Therefore, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8843789.Ultraviolet__Ultraviolet___1_' title='Ultraviolet (Ultraviolet, #1) by R.J. Anderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ultraviolet</a> hovers somewhere halfway</span>
  <span id="freeText4108614888568538293" style="display:none"><b>3 1/2 stars</b><br /><br />I know a whole bunch of my GR friends have heard me say this before but I'm going to say it again for the benefit of any newcomers who stumble across this review: because rating a book can be a tricky process and three stars can mean anything from "I was totally unmoved by it" to "it was pretty good for the most part", I tend to take the GR system literally. By this I mean that three stars is "I liked it" and is a mostly positive rating. Therefore, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8843789.Ultraviolet__Ultraviolet___1_" title="Ultraviolet (Ultraviolet, #1) by R.J. Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Ultraviolet</a> hovers somewhere halfway between "I liked it" and "I really liked it" because there were parts I absolutely loved but also many things that got on my nerves and had me mentally lowering my rating. I will say one thing for certain: I need to read the sequel. NOW.<br /><br />The suspense that Anderson builds up in this book is almost palpable, you find yourself questioning everything and experiencing the frustration of someone who is imprisoned in a mental institution when they feel they are innocent, then later the confusion of someone who begins to doubt their own sanity. Being inside Alison's mind is a scary place to find yourself but, though there is a paranormal element to this novel, you soon find that the author has weaved fact with fiction and incorporated a real-world factor into her story - synesthesia. This is something I had only heard of in passing before I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8843789.Ultraviolet__Ultraviolet___1_" title="Ultraviolet (Ultraviolet, #1) by R.J. Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Ultraviolet</a>, but I have since been inspired to do some more research on the topic. I enjoyed this addition to the novel immensely, simply because it would have been far easier - and what I first expected - to explain away a character's special abilities as some weird supernatural phenomenon.<br /><br />However, Alison's synesthesia leads me perfectly onto what was at times the greatest threat to my enjoyment of the book and at other times what made me go wide-eyed with adoring book love - the prose. Some of it reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a> (but it wasn't that bad or I wouldn't have finished it) and the explanation of synesthesia for the use of colour-based metaphors might make sense but it didn't make it any less annoying for me. Take this:<br /><br /><i>Not only was his voice amazing, so was his name: violet to match his eyes, tranquil and playful at the same time, full of shimmering highlights and unexpected depths. And the Sebastian part wasn't bad either - all oregano and woodsmoke, with a hint of sensuality that made my skin flush just thinking about it.</i><br /><br />and<br /><br /><i>I preferred handwriting, where every loop sent a flush of aquamarine up my arm as though I'd dipped it in a tropic sea.</i><br /><br />and<br /><br /><i>"There. Are. No. Stars," she hissed, her voice full of icy peaks and seething valleys.</i><br /><br />To me, these sentences are not beautiful but eyeroll-worthy. Unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a>, though, the use of them wasn't as constant and I didn't have to hurt myself trying to understand the similes and metaphors. The writing in this book walked a very fine line between stunning and grotesque at times, some passages I could have read over and over for hours without getting tired of them and others made me cringe. To balance out the negative, I wanted to include this little paragraph that I thought was beautiful:<br /><br /><i>I heard the universe as an oratorio sung by a master choir of stars, accompanied by the orchestra of the planets and the percussion of satellites and moons. The aria they performed was a song to break the heart, full of tragic dissonance and deferred hope, and yet somewhere beneath it all was a piercing refrain of glory, glory, glory. And I sensed that not only the grand movements of the cosmos, but everything that had happened in my life, was a part of that song.</i><br /><br />Also, while this novel was highly original for the most part, the romance and the love interest were not. Or at least not for the first two thirds of the book. It began as it usually begins with descriptions of his male perfection, everything from his eyes to his hands to his voice was crafted by the gods, apparently. He is the nicest of the nice, the hottest of the hot... the, um, perfectist of the perfect. Later, he is allowed a few imperfections that help to shape his character and made me like him more but the lack of chemistry at the beginning made it hard to buy into their relationship. Not only that, but it also seemed very inappropriate at first due to the circumstances under which they met.<br /><br />Now, I have to say that I knew what the big twist was before I began this book but I enjoyed it anyway and I don't really think it had much effect on my overall rating. The thing is, it's ridiculously easy to spoil this book for yourself just by looking at its tags and shelves on goodreads - so, you know, try not to glance over to the right side of the page when you add this. Which you totally should do right now. This is a gripping psychological paranormal story that offers a new spin on a very formulaic genre, it is not faultless but it will keep you on the edge of your seat. I am betting that 99% of people who read this will have to read the sequel even if they shared the same problems I had with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4108614888568538293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_155154741" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155154741" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155154741?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Wha-wha-wha-whaaaa?</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Flannery by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=arc-galley-or-first-reads">arc-galley-or-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep">wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155154741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4839485897718298383">Ultraviolet is a genre-bender, there’s no doubt about it, and I don’t think I’ve been this surprised about the direction a book took in quite some time. What I find particularly intriguing is the fact that all of us who’ve read it seem equally stumped as to how to write a review of a book whilst still leaving out half of the plot so as to preserve the experience for other readers--talk about a mighty task. When I originally wrote a placeholder for this review, it basically just said that I wish </span>
  <span id="freeText4839485897718298383" style="display:none">Ultraviolet is a genre-bender, there’s no doubt about it, and I don’t think I’ve been this surprised about the direction a book took in quite some time. What I find particularly intriguing is the fact that all of us who’ve read it seem equally stumped as to how to write a review of a book whilst still leaving out half of the plot so as to preserve the experience for other readers--talk about a mighty task. When I originally wrote a placeholder for this review, it basically just said that I wish I could somehow warn off the subset of readers that might not be on board for the plot twist in this one. It would truly be a shame if the ratings for the book go down due to the alienation. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hah. Alienation. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Then again, I myself was THAT reader who went apeshit at a genre change in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7617119.I_Am_Not_A_Serial_Killer__John_Cleaver___1_" title="I Am Not A Serial Killer (John Cleaver, #1) by Dan Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">I Am Not A Serial Killer</a>. Let’s just say that the setup for the genre switch in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8843789.Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet by R.J. Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Ultraviolet</a> actually has quite a bit of buildup and since I knew we were in a psych ward and things could get trippy, I was game for whatever this author was going to toss my way.<br /><br />I’ve already read two YA books set in psychiatric treatment situations this year—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/534258.Sisters_in_Sanity" title="Sisters in Sanity by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Sisters in Sanity</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3097601.Suicide_Notes" title="Suicide Notes by Michael Thomas Ford" rel="nofollow noopener">Suicide Notes</a>. Turns out, I really like the genre so if you know of any more good ones, shoot the recs to me in the comments. At the onset of this novel, Alison Jeffries wakes up in a psych ward after she fought with Tori, a classmate from school of whom Alison has always been a little suspect. Tori is missing and Alison thinks she might’ve killed her but she’s finding it hard to recollect the details from the event because she suffered some sort of mental overload during and directly afterward. She remembers <i>disintegrating</i> Tori, but that can’t be right, can it? <br /><br />The prose in Ultraviolet is saturated with imagery, and it didn’t bother me too much because there was a reason for it. I don’t want to spoil Alison’s diagnoses but the language and stylistic choices are deliberate and effective at giving readers a glance into what life might be like in Ali’s world. She keeps most of her experiences under tight wraps and that aspect of the book was both fascinating and frustrating. It was fascinating to me to see what it might be like to “fake it”—to completely pretend that the experiences you are having aren’t happening. I can’t pretend to know what it would be like but it must be awful to have no idea if what you are experiencing might be normal. I was happy to see Alison finally open up—it was rough going for a bit there.<br /><br />I truly loved the first half of the book and frankly, I am surprised at myself that I found the second half to be a little weaker because it is right in my wheelhouse. I think I just got so wrapped up in the self-analysis and the murder mystery that when the book turned heavy on the action, my brain just shut off. I still kept fiendishly turning the pages (well, on my Kindle), but I was rather flabbergasted at what was going on. And I hear there’s a sequel in the works? I am happy/sad about that-- happy because I rather enjoyed this one and it will be interesting to see where Ali (and Tori? And maybe even Sebastian?) goes from here, but sad because I thought this was a standalone.<br /><br />I recommend this book to those who are ready for a surprise and those who, whether they like tons of description or not, are willing to give it a chance when it actually has a purpose other than indulgence.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4839485897718298383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8642292662965544317"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471147654ra/20005988.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This one ended up being quite good! The pacing was a bit uneven in the first half, but I quite enjoyed the second part. Alison is 17 and has synesthesia. She senses things in different ways. For example, sounds and letters have colors and she can tell when people are lying because they give off colors and she can taste it. It's a phenomenon that has led to her being insecure, leading an isolated life, and having a strained relationship with her parents. She ends up at a mental hospital following</span>
  <span id="freeText8642292662965544317" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471147654ra/20005988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This one ended up being quite good! The pacing was a bit uneven in the first half, but I quite enjoyed the second part. Alison is 17 and has synesthesia. She senses things in different ways. For example, sounds and letters have colors and she can tell when people are lying because they give off colors and she can taste it. It's a phenomenon that has led to her being insecure, leading an isolated life, and having a strained relationship with her parents. She ends up at a mental hospital following a violent encounter with her mother and police triggered by a traumatic event involving a girl at school that she has no memory of. <br><br>The first half of the book was a bit of this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471147654ra/20005989.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alison interacting with other patients and doctors. She meets a researcher named Dr. Faraday who begins to help her understand her synesthesia and find out more about her abilities. There is a little bit of the "special snowflake" thing going on, but it wasn't overbearing.<br><br>There is one point in the book where everything changes and it becomes a cool sci-fi story. That is the part I liked best. I don't want to spoil it, so I won't say any more, but I thought it was pretty cool.<br><br>I had taken some notes about items I found annoying, but the good news is that they really ended up not mattering because Alison has growth and resolution with her mother (who I hated for half the book) and other characters she had conflicts with.<br><br>The supporting characters were a bit one-dimensional, but I quite liked Dr. Faraday and Tori. <br><br>I almost DNF'd this but am glad I did not. I think it was written well and is one of the better YAs I've read recently.<br><br>SPOILER through end of the book.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was a bit convenient that the aliens looked just like humans except for silver hair and slightly different skin tone, but I was able to overlook it. I wanted Dr. Faraday to be able to come back to earth, but at the same time, it felt right because I don't think it was realistic for him to be with Alison, who was only 17. Their romance felt a little weird because of the age difference and him being in a position of authority. I think he was supposed to be "really young" for a scientist, but still.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_171426089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171426089?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=postcard-from-outer-space">postcard-from-outer-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=never-saw-it-coming">never-saw-it-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171426089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10723764515156075454">I'm always a little hesitant to review the books I loved. It seems like nothing I write can ever be good enough. That's exactly the case this time. I'll try to keep it short and very clear: this book blew me away! <br/>It took only about 30 pages for me to fall in love with Ultraviolet. If I remember correctly, I called Anderson's writing unpretentious and rich with emotion when I just started reading, and I stand by my words now that I've finished. What amazed me the most about it was the way she oc</span>
  <span id="freeText10723764515156075454" style="display:none">I'm always a little hesitant to review the books I loved. It seems like nothing I write can ever be good enough. That's exactly the case this time. I'll try to keep it short and very clear: this book blew me away! <br />It took only about 30 pages for me to fall in love with Ultraviolet. If I remember correctly, I called Anderson's writing unpretentious and rich with emotion when I just started reading, and I stand by my words now that I've finished. What amazed me the most about it was the way she occasionally threw a stunning passage or a breathtaking sentence into what was normally pretty simplistic writing. <br /><br /><i> Dark chocolate, poured over with velvet: that was how his voice tasted. I wanted him to follow me around and narrate the rest of my life.</i><br /><br />I'm not a visual type of person, but words mean the world to me, and R.J. Anderson's words made a strong impression. The way Alison perceives the world made me want to be her, if just for ten minutes, and experience things and people through her eyes (and her mouth). Tasting words sounds like something I would gladly live with for the rest of my life!<br /><br /><i>I’d been trying to get over my habit of judging people by the color and taste of their names, but it was hard when my instincts were so often right. There seemed no point telling myself that the R in the middle of Kirk’s name didn’t make him untrustworthy when the game had just started and he was already cheating.</i><br /><br />And then the major plot twist happened. I was a bit annoyed at first because I really liked the way the story was originally going, but after a while, I started to like the new development too, which only proves how amazing R.J. Anderson really is. <br /><br />Another small thing I really liked was the lack of Ali's physical description. I know nothing about the color of her hair, the length of her eyelashes or the way she blushes when she's embarrassed and I like it that way. It was very refreshing not to be bothered with unimportant things like that. <br /><br />Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7094569.Feed__Newsflesh___1_" title="Feed (Newsflesh, #1) by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Feed</a> has made me reluctant to give five stars as easily as I did before, but they're well deserved this time. <br />I have such high hopes for this book! I hope people will recognize its beauty and its literary value. R.J. Anderson has gained a new fan - I'm ready to read everything she's ever written, including her grocery lists. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10723764515156075454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-e-i-will-always-love-you">i-e-i-will-always-love-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=cried-my-eyes-out">cried-my-eyes-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-will-have-children-with-this-book">i-will-have-children-with-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308211649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16567827414993998576">This book and I are eloping. It's settled and there's nothing you can do to stop it. No, seriously. We've planned the eloping and everything. Go find another book to elope with. <i>Ultraviolet</i> is mine. Forever and ever. But not in a creepy way, or anything like that... *awkward laugh*<br/><br/>It's been three days still I finished <i>Ultraviolet</i>, and I still cannot think coherently. Honestly, it's a miracle I can form full sentences at this point. If my incoherency, eloping, or rating weren't a clear indication</span>
  <span id="freeText16567827414993998576" style="display:none">This book and I are eloping. It's settled and there's nothing you can do to stop it. No, seriously. We've planned the eloping and everything. Go find another book to elope with. <i>Ultraviolet</i> is mine. Forever and ever. But not in a creepy way, or anything like that... *awkward laugh*<br><br>It's been three days still I finished <i>Ultraviolet</i>, and I still cannot think coherently. Honestly, it's a miracle I can form full sentences at this point. If my incoherency, eloping, or rating weren't a clear indication, I love this book. A lot, actually. Does it have its problems? Of course. Every book has its problems. Do I care? No. <br><br>I will tiptoe very, <i>very</i> lightly around writing this synopsis, because I'm afraid anything in this book can be a spoiler. Actually, I don't trust myself writing a synopsis for <i>Ultraviolet</i>. All you need to know is that it's about a young teenager named Alison who is convicted of killing a girl in her school by disintegrating her with her mind, and she is currently in a mental hospital. Then things happen. <br><br>"Then things happen." Man, I have such a way with words. <br><br>Aaaaanyway, I should really start wrapping up this review, or whatever I should call this, so that you don't have to suffer through any more of my incoherency.<br><br>The bottom line is this: <i>Ultraviolet</i> is a thoroughly brilliant novel, and it is gorgeously written. As for the problems I mentioned earlier, sure, this book has some. For starters, it has an unnecessary romance that <i>could</i> be taken as insta-love, and Alison and her love interest are saying their 'I love you's' not long after they meet. Normally that would be more than enough for a book to lose a star for in my rating system, but I honestly can't make myself give <i>Ultraviolet</i> any less than five stars. It's not a perfect book, but it's perfect for <i>me</i>, and I sincerely hope it is the same for you as well. But don't love this book too much, because we've eloped and that could cause some problems. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374427ra/728441.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>....<br><br><b>Pre-Review:</b> [Do <b>not</b>, under any circumstances, click on the spoiler if you haven't yet read <i>Ultraviolet</i>. Yes, I'm talking to you, you spoiler clicker.]<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374427i/728442.jpg" width="239" height="239" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I had to. <br><br><s>Incoherent babbling</s> er, I mean, my review, or at least what I hope will eventually take the form of a review, and not just ... you know, incoherent babbling ... to come. Maybe. <br><br>Oh, who am I kidding? This review will be incoherent babble and you know it. <br><br>Bottom line: I loved <i>Ultraviolet</i> with a passion. It's probably my favorite read of 2012 so far. Read it. Love it. Then come back and click the spoiler. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

Anderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ultraviolet</a> is a five star book. <br/><br/>Or, at least the first 230ish <i>pages</i> are from a five star book and the remaining few chapters belong in WTF Capital City. But more on that later.<br/><br/>Initially, be prepared to be sucked in to the weaving vortex that is Ultraviolet. From the get go we are presented with a puzzle the likes of which I have not experienced in a long time. <br/><br/>There's nothing worse than when a mystery isn't, you know, mys</span>
  <span id="freeText631076959405827540" style="display:none"><br>In the interest of staying fair to R.J.Anderson I will make it clear that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8843789.Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet by R.J. Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Ultraviolet</a> is a five star book. <br><br>Or, at least the first 230ish <i>pages</i> are from a five star book and the remaining few chapters belong in WTF Capital City. But more on that later.<br><br>Initially, be prepared to be sucked in to the weaving vortex that is Ultraviolet. From the get go we are presented with a puzzle the likes of which I have not experienced in a long time. <br><br>There's nothing worse than when a mystery isn't, you know, mysterious as mysteries should be. Luckily, this is not the case with Ultraviolet, which is evident when we reflect on my inner monologue:<br><br><i>"Why is she there? What’s going to happen? WHERE ARE WE GOING? This is awesome. What is the significance of THAT I wonder? I AM SO INTREEEEEEEEGUED! <br>Who did it? I don’t know. Any chance it was... Could it have been... was it... <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351370i/705019.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>... the MUFFIN MAN???"</i><br><br><br>I HAD NO IDEA! And I was happily going along with the ride until, all of a sudden, out of NOWHERE, this happens: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[GUESS WHAT! WE ARE ALL ALIENS <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and now here we are in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[OUTER SPACE! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><br><br>...<br><br><br>*crickets*<br><br><br>...<br><br><br>Um. Excuse me. But.... WHAT? <br><br>I’m all for books throwing me a curve ball but that was just ridiculous. I mean, LOST ridiculous:<br><br><i>So there was a plane crash on an island. And then came the</i> others <i> along with their smoke monster and then there was a polar bear massacre and then John ate an orange and we did a bit of time travel and then there was a big stone foot and then...</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351370i/705020.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I think I need to lie down.<br><br><br>And so I am presented with a conundrum. Because I have not been this absorbed in anything since <a href="http://pastaqueen.com/halfofme/images/apollo_built.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">Apollo lost his towel</a>, if you know what I’m saying. <br><br>But on the other hand I wish I had been consulted when Anderson decided to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[take the party into space <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> because she appears to have been smoking some serious green. <br><br>But don’t let me put you off. It's still a five star book. <br>...even though I've only given it four.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_3557094837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3557094837" />
    <a title="Merphy Napier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier"><img alt="Merphy Napier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524921716p2/41973734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3557094837?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merphy Napier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merphy Napier" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier">Merphy Napier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=three-stars">three-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3557094837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7796739794635902033">I have no idea how to review this book. <br/><br/>The first two thirds were around 4 stars, the last third was closer to a 2. So here I land at 3. <br/><br/>The driving mystery of this book and the slow unraveling was so much fun to read. Then you have the really unique *thing* that was introduced <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ synesthesia  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was really interesting as well. <br/><br/>However, while the twist was something that I could see people either loving or hating, I was really okay with it. If it had been executed well.</span>
  <span id="freeText7796739794635902033" style="display:none">I have no idea how to review this book. <br /><br />The first two thirds were around 4 stars, the last third was closer to a 2. So here I land at 3. <br /><br />The driving mystery of this book and the slow unraveling was so much fun to read. Then you have the really unique *thing* that was introduced <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ synesthesia  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was really interesting as well. <br /><br />However, while the twist was something that I could see people either loving or hating, I was really okay with it. If it had been executed well. But honestly, there were several elements that were, in my opinion, sloppy. Plus the romance was gross.<br /><br />Sloppy stuff: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ there's several things I could mention but I'll just do one. There was a mental patient that said Faraday was having sex with her after he was fired. Not only is that incredibly inappropriate, but that SHOULD bother our MC. The thing though is that Allison cared in that scene, then she seemed to forget all about it. I kept waiting for it to be addressed again, but it never was! Allison didn't even ask Faraday after they got together! It's like she forgot! Actually, it honestly read like the author put it in there to add drama but then forgot to bring it up again. There were several things like this that either seemed to slip through the cracks, or the way it was resolved was done in a really unnatural way (like when Faraday tried to give Kirk's backstory to Allison after her sexual assault to give her closer but he wasn't even there for the incident and the convo came out of nowhere).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Romance: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I'll keep this short. Or try. She was 16 and his age was never actually stated in the book, but based of his level of education and experience, I'll guess mid 20s. As if that isn't enough, the *entirety* of their relationship was established while she was in a mental institute, and he was in charge of her study. The whole time they knew each other, pretty much up until the moment they got together, she was in an incredibly vulnerable state, and he was in a position of power and authority over her. He even admits in the end that she's too young for him and he allowed himself to forget it for a while. Thing is, this wasn't depicted as a terrible thing that (sadly) happens in real life sometimes, it was just a normal romance that we're supposed to fall for too. Nah.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Basically, I it was a great build up, with a really interesting mystery and slow unraveling, but when it came time for everything to be revealed, it was pretty choppy in the way it was done. Plus a romance that never should have happened (esp in a YA). So I enjoyed reading it until the end. And I'm a bit bummed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7796739794635902033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167624409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167624409" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167624409?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780761374084" href="/book/show/10634910-ultraviolet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=strange">strange</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-really-enjoyed-it">i-really-enjoyed-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-favs">2011-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=original-and-creative">original-and-creative</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167624409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7623081465335405166"><br/><i>Ultraviolet</i> was such a pleasant surprise! I've been thinking about this review for a few days because it's hard to say something about it without giving too much away. It's one of those books that you just have to go in knowing absolutely nothing. So, I will try my best to keep this short and sweet. :)<br/><br/><i>Ultraviolet</i> is about a girl named Alison who ends up in a mental institute after she has a psychotic break, during which she confesses to murdering a fellow classmate. What makes this book so cool </span>
  <span id="freeText7623081465335405166" style="display:none"><br /><i>Ultraviolet</i> was such a pleasant surprise! I've been thinking about this review for a few days because it's hard to say something about it without giving too much away. It's one of those books that you just have to go in knowing absolutely nothing. So, I will try my best to keep this short and sweet. :)<br /><br /><i>Ultraviolet</i> is about a girl named Alison who ends up in a mental institute after she has a psychotic break, during which she confesses to murdering a fellow classmate. What makes this book so cool is that she has synesthesia, a neurological phenomenon, which allows her to see sounds and taste colors. <br /><br />The way Anderson wove this beautiful story had me mesmerized. I fell in love with the way Alison described the world in her senses. I seriously felt like I was watching the Aurora Borealis while reading <i>Ultraviolet</i>. <br /><br />The plot was solid and left the reader to catch up to the mystery surrounding her classmate's death. I really enjoyed that because it added to the suspense. I will say that the plot twist was a tad predictable. There was quite a bit of foreshadowing going on, so it wasn't hard to see where things were going. BUT that did not stop me from really enjoying this book and the ending did surprise me.<br /><br />Things were tied up nicely in this book at the end, but in this case I'm really hoping there will be a sequel. And I eagerly look forward to any other books from R.J. Anderson!<br /><br />More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7623081465335405166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3742163944570186527">Awesome! <br/><br/>Ultraviolet is so incredibly original. It was an absolute pleasure to read. The writing is well crafted, elegant, colorful, and beautifully descriptive. It has a captivating quality and I was hooked right from the start. <br/><br/>Ultraviolet is the story of a very special teenage girl. Alison finds herself in a psychiatric hospital ward. She believes that she caused a classmate to disintegrate. When the classmate goes missing, Alison confesses to the murder even though no body has been found. <br/><br/>Al</span>
  <span id="freeText3742163944570186527" style="display:none">Awesome! <br /><br />Ultraviolet is so incredibly original. It was an absolute pleasure to read. The writing is well crafted, elegant, colorful, and beautifully descriptive. It has a captivating quality and I was hooked right from the start. <br /><br />Ultraviolet is the story of a very special teenage girl. Alison finds herself in a psychiatric hospital ward. She believes that she caused a classmate to disintegrate. When the classmate goes missing, Alison confesses to the murder even though no body has been found. <br /><br />Alison has special abilities. She sees numbers in color. She tastes shapes. Music becomes fireworks in her head. Sensations such as pleasure and pain are in color. Alison thinks she is going crazy until a researcher gives a name to her condition – synesthesia. At this point, I couldn’t help myself. I started googling this condition. Fascinating!<br /><br />The story is told from Alison’s point of view. The reader only knows as much as Alison does. The author doles out little bits of information sparingly like pieces of a jigsaw puzzle, keeping the reader in suspense throughout the novel. It really kept me guessing.<br /><br />Suddenly, the story changes. It’s almost like you are reading another book, not in a bad way, just different. And it works, it really does. <br /><br />Ultraviolet is an intelligent young adult novel. There are no love triangles, no real angst, just a young girl trying to find her place in this world. This book made me feel a purplish shade of blue. <br /><br />I’m looking forward to reading more of R. J. Anderson’s books in the future.<br /><br /><i>* ARC provided free of charge from Netgalley</i><br /><br /><b>Ultraviolet has been featured as a Badass Hidden Gems - Canada eh? edition book <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com/badass-hidden-gems-canada-eh-and-giveaway-too/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a></b></span>

<div id="review_314256423" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/314256423" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4089478-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315759484p2/4089478.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/314256423?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/4089478-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780761374084" href="/book/show/10634910-ultraviolet">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jim by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=kindle-books">kindle-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=wendy-said">wendy-said</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer314256423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6916513140989512347">***I have tried to avoid spoilers. If you have read the book, you know how difficult that can be in this case. If you haven’t, you might be well advised to just check it out first, and come back to the reviews later... I REALLY liked it, and will try to walk the tightrope of discussing it without giving it away..<br/>///////<br/><br/>There is a key moment very early in this book - a flashback to Alison at age 6. She is watching her mom washing dishes, and seeing a trail of gold stars when the cutlery clinks. T</span>
  <span id="freeText6916513140989512347" style="display:none">***I have tried to avoid spoilers. If you have read the book, you know how difficult that can be in this case. If you haven’t, you might be well advised to just check it out first, and come back to the reviews later... I REALLY liked it, and will try to walk the tightrope of discussing it without giving it away..<br />///////<br /><br />There is a key moment very early in this book - a flashback to Alison at age 6. She is watching her mom washing dishes, and seeing a trail of gold stars when the cutlery clinks. This visual sensation is very beautiful to Alison, but she has no idea that there is anything unusual about it.<br /><br />She asks for more of the gold stars, and the shock of her mom’s violent and angry reaction is a defining moment in Alison’s life. Her mom’s orders are very clear. There are No stars. Alison is never to mention them, or anything like them to anyone, ever! People will think she is crazy! Allison’s mom thinks so too, while her dad is intelligent but basically clueless on this issue:<br /><br /><i>“My father was a sweet man, but most of the time he acted like his body was only there to keep his brain from dragging on the ground.”</i><br /><br />For Alison, this moment changes everything about her relations with other people. She can never reveal those special perceptions. But they continue and grow more complex as she reaches her teens, a product of some unusual circuitry in her brain and eyes. (I will save other comments on this point for later discussion, if others are interested)<br /><br /><i>“You know how when some people first take up painting they don’t know how to mix colors properly, and all their pictures end up looking all garish and cheap? It’s like that when I watch TV.” </i><br /><br />I bought into Alison’s defining, traumatic moment - it made sense to me. A childhood trauma takes away the simple joy of a beautiful set of perceptions, and turns them into a continuing nightmare. Intimidated by her mother’s outraged warning, Alison lives and builds much of her life around these perceptions, but knows she must keep them hidden or society will cast her aside.<br /><br />But what drives much of the story is an even more horrifying turn of events, and the aftermath of this incident puts her in the psychiatric institution that her mother had feared all along. The book begins with her in this institution, piecing together the story (in first person) through her own deep confusion about what really happened, and what is or is not wrong with her. This confusion is a core element of the story - it makes everything she sees, thinks and does highly suspicious, to herself and to everyone around her.<br /><br /><i>“So I pushed the bitterness down, into the black pit of my stomach along with my regret and my grief and my fear, and I said, “I’m fine. May I go now?” “</i><br /><br />The plot twists and turns from this point, and pieces/parts have been carefully indicated in all the reviews that I read. Nearly all of it worked extremely well for me. Having bought into the tortured but exotic inner world of Allison, I was prepared for the tortuous saga that followed. I anticipated some of the twists, though certainly not all. But I enjoyed the story greatly, right through to the end.<br /><br />Your mileage may vary. A lot of trusted reviewers/friends had issues with this one, and it may just not work for you. What is really tricky is that serious readers will react in very different ways to the characters and the twists. I get that. <br /><br />Here is the way I think of it. I love authors who can define a 'world' and make it work. Authors who follow their artistic vision and put it out there as they see it. The world could be almost anything - physical, psychological, pure fantasy, etc. And yes, things can change dramatically as the story rolls along.<br /><br />For me, the ‘success’ of that world is not so much about what is in it, or even how it works, but how skillful the author is in depicting it. What I am judging is whether the creation hangs together for me. Is it internally consistent? Is the writing clear and moving? Do I care about the characters? Does the story gain momentum and then hold it? <br /><br />In the hands of a lesser writer, I don't think that any part of this story would have drawn me in or held my interest. But Anderson’s writing scored strong positives on all of my criteria. I raced through it to see what would happen next. My pulse was pounding at many points in the story. In the end, I cared strongly about several of the characters and was satisfied with the outcome. <br /><br />Thinking back, what I really enjoyed throughout was the skillful maneuvering of observation, inference and the unsettling new facts. For me, it was a marvelous excursion to see events unfold through the lens of Alison’s confusion, mental instability and her extraordinary perceptions. I was particularly impressed by the deft handling of shifting relationships among the characters, as the stereotyped certainties of one chapter became the deeper and more complex truths of the next. I would definitely read it again.<br /><br /><b>Very Highly Recommended.</b><br /><br />Special thanks to Wendy Darling for her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170824273" rel="nofollow noopener"> excellent review</a> and recommendation. <br /><br />There are many other exceptional reviews of this book, but the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170719450" rel="nofollow noopener"> one by Crowinator</a> really resonated with my own take.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6916513140989512347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_170719450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170719450" />
    <a title="Crowinator" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator"><img alt="Crowinator" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604950964p2/283407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170719450?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crowinator" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crowinator" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator">Crowinator</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780761374084" href="/book/show/10634910-ultraviolet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=genre-science-fiction">genre-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=ra-ya-sff">ra-ya-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=aliens-spaceships-space">aliens-spaceships-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=unreliable-narrators">unreliable-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=favorites-2011">favorites-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170719450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8367370140107882166">I love me an unreliable narrator, particularly when you can’t identify what kind of unreliable he or she is. Is he sincere in his beliefs but crazy? Is she a pathological liar? Is he a con man intentionally deceiving his audience? Is she just out of the loop, a narrator who thinks she knows what’s going on but is actually being tricked by others? I stayed up until almost midnight to finish this in a marathon reading session, and I found it an incredibly addictive genre-bender.<br/><br/>Alison is set up as</span>
  <span id="freeText8367370140107882166" style="display:none">I love me an unreliable narrator, particularly when you can’t identify what kind of unreliable he or she is. Is he sincere in his beliefs but crazy? Is she a pathological liar? Is he a con man intentionally deceiving his audience? Is she just out of the loop, a narrator who thinks she knows what’s going on but is actually being tricked by others? I stayed up until almost midnight to finish this in a marathon reading session, and I found it an incredibly addictive genre-bender.<br /><br />Alison is set up as suspect right from the start, from the moment she wakes up in a sterile hospital room, arms covered in self-inflicted scratches, missing a bunch of memories and pressed with the uncomfortable feeling that something’s gone terribly wrong. The fact that she’s been involuntarily committed after a psychotic episode doesn’t surprise her as much as it should, and the policeman who escorts her, hand-cuffed, to her new home in a private psych ward for teenagers seems to think she knows something about a classmate’s disappearance. The missing girl, Tori, had an argument with Alison just before disappearing, and it was no secret they disliked each other – but did Alison do something to warrant this suspicious treatment? And do her family and friends and the doctors at the institution really want to help her, or do they all have ulterior motives?<br /><br />Alison has always worried about being a little crazy because of the different way her mind perceives things: letters, numbers, names, and sounds have colors and emotions and even tastes associated with them. Telling lies taste bad and make her sick; hopefulness in someone’s voice tastes like powdered sugar; the ringing sound dishes make while washing make stars burst before her eyes; people’s names hold clues to their personality, based on the qualities of the letters. It gives her narrative an unusual sensory rich quality without being overdone or unreadable, and Anderson does an amazing job using language to convey how Alison experiences the world. Plus, being so firmly in Alison’s head makes it hard to doubt her – everything is colored by her odd perceptions, and she seems so sincere and honest – but also impossible to fully believe she knows the true story, either. <br /><br />She’s been taught by her mother to keep her unusual perceptions a secret, to be ashamed of it, but it’s a real condition (and I don’t feel this is a spoiler, because even the publisher’s marketing mentions it) called <i>synesthesia</i>. Because I already knew this, I was predisposed to think that Alison wasn’t really crazy – she just didn’t know that there was a real explanation. But then, the more she starts remembering the events of the night Tori disappeared, the more unstable she seems, especially when she flat out admits to herself that she disintegrated Tori with the power of her mind. <br /><br />Right at that moment, this book took me in wholly, because that’s when I had to admit I had no idea where Anderson was going to take this story. The best part of reading this book is trying to figure out, as Alison sorts through her memories and gets drawn into the lives of the other patients in the ward, what really happened that night. Did Alison kill Tori? And did Tori disintegrate, or is Alison just crazy? If she did disintegrate, what the hell does that mean? There is honestly no way to predict, for sure, where the story is going to go without spoilers. This is coming from someone who considers it her particular superpower to make those predictions and be right 98% of the time (what, even someone with superpowers can’t be right ALL of the time). <br /><br />The book starts off as a realistic story taking place in a mental institution, but evidence stacks up, in a subtle way, that something supernatural is going on; the problem is, since we’re reading from Alison’s point of view, there’s no way of knowing if her gathering evidence that points to something otherworldly is legit. There are a lot of promising clues that turn out to be red herrings, and little moments that turn out in retrospect to be clues, while characters you like turn out to be skeevy and vice versa. The later piece of the novel, where the slow-building tension pays off and turns to straight-up action, is surprising and will put off some readers and make others squee with delight (I am one of the second ones). I did feel the transition was a little abrupt, but maybe that’s because it doesn’t get a lot of expansion compared with the rest of the story, which takes up more than half, and because it moves super fast in comparison; I think these later developments will be more focused in on book two.<br /><br />I feel like I can’t discuss the plot anymore without ruining it, even though I’m leaving out a major character/love interest. Of course just saying there’s a major tonal shift is sort of setting up new readers for the experience, but that can be a good thing, too. Still, this genre-bender wouldn’t be nearly so successful without Anderson’s great writing. There are so many quotable descriptive moments, like Alison’s descriptions that are spot-on and often hilarious (for example, she introduces Tori by saying, “And where the new girl had curves, I had angles and despair”; and she introduces another person by describing his clothes as “exciting shades like Old Filing Cabinet and Dryer Lint”). <br /><br />Another plus is the ensemble cast – while this book is really all about Alison for most of the time, her fellow patients, her mother and father, the doctors and nurses and orderlies, and a certain potential love interest, all have enough depth to hint that there’s more going on with them than Alison realizes. They are believable background players, and when a few of them move into the spotlight, they become as complex as Alison. <br /><br />Sheer curiosity kept me turning the pages -- I had to know what really happened to Alison and Tori -- but the writing made it worthwhile, and I admire Anderson for really going there with the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ It's not every day that an author takes a fairly realistic story and turns it into a balls-out alien conspiracy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Can't wait to read the next one!<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8367370140107882166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
